<username>Luis Toral<//username><Date>1612819481653<//Date><rate>5<//rate>< review>
Haters could hate, but the crab zone is a force to be reckoned with. I spoke with the owner's son on why it was so pricey. It was because of the cost to sustain the crawfish. The crawfish is very difficult to sustain, so they have to bump up the price in order to be able to keep it for long. It is fresh, but cmon, you can't complain about the service since there is a LITERAL CHILD COOKING FOR YOU. I am not friends with the owner (Yeah i'm talking to you person who said anyone over 3 stars is friends with the owner), but would 100% recommend.<//review>

My experience was almost like one of the other reviews. I wanted crab for my birthday dinner and my wife and son took me to The Crab Zone. Mistake!!!! It was very high priced and the service was p-poor. The waitress was more interested in trimming the plants than trending our table. There was one other table with 2 customers. The music was too loud and when talking to the waitress we had to have her repeat herself several times. My hearing is not good but my wife and son can hear fine. They couldn't hear her over the music.

There are many different types of music and my son enjoys many of them. He told me the music was terrible. That makes a statement from an 18 year old young man.

I asked if the one crab would be enough for the three of us. Her statement was it depends on how hungry you are. OK. I get that. One small plastic cup for a beverage and that was it. Didn't ask if we wanted more to drink or eat.

I would refer Denny's before this place. At least you get more than one drink and the waiters and waitress can speak so you can hear them.<//text>

We were nervous we wouldnt be served because of reading other reviews abou their service time policy. We were greated by the owner and sat immediately. < review>
Made a reservation for three for my parents and I here on a weekend right after they opened up for dinner. The place was quite empty as they'd just opened, but slowly (not obnoxiously) filled up with [mostly older?] people. The interior of the space is gorgeous. Classic Southern decor with a modern exposed kitchen in the back.

The service was really fantastic. Definitely top 10 service experiences. And it felt really genuine too; didn't get the fake personality vibe from anyone.

The food was all perfect. We shared all our plates. The mussels were amazing. The cheese plate was wonderful. A bit pricey, but definitely worth it.

Also note: they have a killer wine selection.</review>

I have mixed feelings about this place. The ambiance was great - I felt like I was in another country and I really liked the decor. On the other hand, neither the service, including hostess or server, or food was mind-blowing, and it was a bit pricey for the experience. 1559331280967</time>
<rating>5< /rating>< Text>
What a treat - honestly this might be my new hangout spot. I didn't have a reservation but the hostess promised to squeeze me in at the bar. The place was quiet and half empty at first but sure enough 15mins went by and it was PACKED. I mean people were being turned down left and right. We finally got sat at the bar and waited about 20mins for service, but the server promptly noticed we hadn't been greeted and offered us complementary glasses of wine. We didn't put up that big of a fight, and the rest of the night was amazing.

The food is brilliantly paired with balancing tastes and flowing wine. The scallops were cooked perfectly and the gnocchi was probably one of the best I've ever tasted. The portions are small but take it slow and you'll be full by the end of the night. We split everything for two and ordered 5 dishes - PERFECTION in every bite.

The chef personally came over to deliver each dish and told us to wait for the ceviche to finish marinating. I'm so glad we did because once again it was well worth any wait.

I will be back to try and taste more and hope that each time I can feel right at home in this cozy little Cafe.<//Text>

< Review>
Fun, buzzy, casual place. We joined in the atmosphere by ordering deserts first, then mains, then starters and no-one was the least bit fazed. First rate wine list with some amazing heirloom (sic) vintages, we drank Henzel 1975 pinot noir and an impressive Dunn cab sav from 1985. Yes, there was food too and I think it was good, but my recollection is rather impaired by the impact of the wine. LOL. Thought the staff were interesting and interested, they added wit and wisdom to the experience. Thank God for uber, Heirloom is a bit off the beaten track but I'd walk it, indeed I'd crawl back if I had to, it was really that good.< /Review>

< Review>
Came here for dinner w my guy.
The goods - very friendly staff and warm cozy lovely atmosphere.
The bad - tiny servings for a hefty price, and over-reliance on heavily salting the dishes, rather than the delicate flavors of food.
My boyfriend had the mushroom fettuccini which was composed of a small palm size serving of pasta and ONE mushroom sliced thinly.
I had the seafood cioppino - very very salty to the point of not being able to eat the broth!!! There was a dozen small mussels and 1 oz (possibly 1.5) of cod in the seafood mixture.  No shrimp nor scallops.
Fettuccini $27, Cioppino $30.
Suffice to say, we left the restaurant feeling hungry ;(.< /Review>

<Review>One of the best meals I've had in SF.

We started with two cheeses: both soft, creamy and surprisingly mild. Other appetizers were the burrata and scallops. For mains we split the gnocchi, hallibut, and burger (cooked with cheeses in the meats). All were equally stellar.

We had the recommended red wine: a metallic Pinot Grigio. Sharp on the tongue with a light finish. Perfect complement to the rich food.

Service was fine.

Ambiance was louder than expected but we were a group of three and they seated us at the end of a communal table and it worked perfectly. Conversation was intimate and we could drown out the rest of the noise.

Update after second meal here: just as god as before, but I was note conscious of how small the portions were this time.</Review>< Pictures>

< Text>
Short version: it's good, it's expensive.  It might not be entirely fair to call it out as expensive, since what really made it more expensive than other similar places is that we got a lot more wine than we usually do.  But the restaurant is especially known for its wine, and they offer excellent pairings, so if you're not going to get the wine, why go?

Great food, great friendly, attentive, but unobtrusive service, nice semi-fancy, semi-rustic atmosphere.  And the wine was great.  It's always eye-opening for me to have wine well paired with food. I ordered a 2005 Rioja when we sat down, and we thought it was OK.  Later in the meal, the same wine came paired with my husband's entree (braised pork, polenta, maple-glazed delicata squash, orange-pecan gremolata) and it was 10 times better.  And with dessert we had a 2011 Juran√ßon Uroulat that was fantastic.

If we were in the mood to have someone hand-hold us through some excellent wines that can't be easily had other places.  But otherwise, for the money, we'd go to Blue Plate or Serpentine.</Text>

< review>
My rescue jack russell/poodle mix Davey is nervous around new people and bringing him in because of an injury doubled that nervousness. I myself was also very nervous since I do not have great prior experience with vets. The reception team - Jennifer and Jessica I believe - were calm and collected over the phone and kind and attentive in person. They helped this nervous dog mom keep my head and gave Davey a few treats to help him settle. Dr. Padilla was amazing with Davey (and me lol). She explained everything in terms I could understand and recommended some future treatment without me feeling pressured to do it right then - even offered me a sample sheet of costs so I could budget it. She talked to Davey through the whole appointment and he took to her quite well. Again, he did have an injury on his side that did turn out to be infected and given that Davey was a previously homeless dog - his instinct did kick in right at the end (thankfully after she'd gotten a sample) and he tried to snap at her. I was so nervous that would be the end of our lovely time here. But Dr. Padilla just rolled with it and let Davey calm down and gave him pets and eventually a treat - letting him know she was rewarding him calming down and not the snapping which I thought was very sweet. And then we moved on with the appointment. It wasn't mentioned again and I wasn't made to feel bad for my dog reacting. Both Dr. Padilla and our "nurse" (who's name is escaping me I'm sorry!) we're patient to my questions and explained the medications Davey needed to me and the reasons behind them and went over costs with me when I explained I had recently started a new job. By the time I paid the bill I was no longer scared or nervous and neither was Davey. We were treated so well here and with so much kindness and gentleness. After years of avoiding vets because of prior bad experience I can finally say I've found a permanent vet for my pets. Thank you all so very much.</review>

< text>
Today was the annual garden vegetable plant sale. The prices were good for a wide variety of tomatoes, corn, herbs, chiles, okra, cabbage, lettuce, you name it they had it. There were also seeds and cow compost for sale. Hand made items were on sale by a large variety of vendors. Many of the historical homes and museums were open, and the Pacific hotel ice cream shop was also selling ice cream. There were several food trucks and carts selling food for lunch. It was a warm sunny day and the History park was packed, but parking was not bad and walking around was pleasant. There were many friendly people and many master gardeners dispensing advice on the plants they were selling. I bought three varieties of tomatoes and three varieties of chiles. The prices were 3 for $10, which is a good deal. It is best to come early as the plans sell out quickly. Awesome event is held annualy.</text>

<Review>(Translated by Google) The story of San Jos√© is brought to a living museum. People can be shown through reenactment and exhibition or with help. The blacksmith uses tools to show how they were used for forming, bending and forging. The print shop shows how printers worked with type, ink and machine-made newspaper printing. Some of the exhibition collections such as steam tractors and locomotives are still in good condition. Also schools come here to get to know the former way. The people here are very friendly and helpful. They explain very nicely what you can do. The terrain is not big, if you just want to look at it, I think you're done in 2 hours. But you have a lot more fun when you also work with and practically learn.
************************************************** *****
The story of San Jose is brought to a living museum. People can be seen through reenactment and exhibition or with help. The blacksmith shows by means of tools how they were used for forming and forging. The printer shows how printers with the type of ink and machine-made newspaper printing were used. Some of the exhibition collections look for steam tractors and locomotives are still in good condition. So schools come here to know the former way. The people here are very friendly and helpful. They explain very nicely what you can do. The terrain is not big, if you just want to look at it, I think you're done in 2 hours. But you have a lot more fun if you work with and learn.

I am not the type of person that likes complaining or giving bad reviews but sometimes that is the last resource you are left with. The food is not the issue here but their customer service. We have been there only three times. The first time we were a big group so we didn't mind it took a bit long to get served. The second time it took about 15-20 for someone to approach us and offer menus and drinks, again we didn't mind since we were having a nice conversation. We were 4 adults. The las time it was tonight 09/27/19. Oh my, tonight was the worst. I do want to make clear that we did notice they were understaffed. Anyways, we waited for 20 minutes without anyone even acknowledging we were there. I see the waitress and ask her for menus, she said give one minute, 10 minutes passed and she didn't approached us, my brother asks again and she finally approaches. She tell us with an attitude, "I am understaffed, I don't have any menus and I have other tables. At this point we say ok, we stand up and start to leave, she says whatever and approaches another table and asks; have you been helped? My family is already at the door but that made me mad so I asked if there are any business cards, she turns around and says no. We do not work with business cards. I say ok, can you tell me your managers name? She answers, she is not here today and you don't need to call her. At this point I can see she is upset and starts to get defensive telling me she already explained she is understaffed and busy. I tell her, I understand and that she does not need to raise her voice, to calm down. She starts talking over me to tell me again she is busy, understaffed etc etc. At this point everyone is looking at us and the last thing I tell her before walking out is. I understand honey, we are leaving not because we waited for too long but because you didn't even acknowledge us, not even to let us know that you saw us, to let us know you were busy and that you were going to be with us as soon as if was possible for you. I walked out after that. The reason we are never going back is the fact that she didn't even looked at us once before I approached her the first time and that was after 20 minutes of being sitting there.</text>

< review>
This particular Marshall's on Bascom in the Pruneyard has always been one of my favorites.  I can usually walk in there and find any number of goodies to satisfy my retail therapy session.  The store is well-organized and relativey neat and clean. It's hard to keep these place looking like a fancy boutique, but the staff do a good job of trying.  Each store has it's uniqueness and this one has a great shoe department for women.  I was in there in the last month and picked up a few tops for summer wear.  Love Marshall's family of stores. One thing about this store is that parking can be challenging especially since the entire center has been in renovation for over two years.  Things are calming down, but this store's parking area is relatively small.< /review>

The selection is out of this world, I asked a worker if I could take some pictures and he said "go ahead, take video if you want."  Super friendly and nice.  Very personable. < Review>
The reason for this 5-star review of Gerrard's is because of Tom (owner/manager). I hadn't known Tom prior to this experience, but he really did something special for me:

On Christmas Eve, I was running around town and had managed to get the gifts that I had planned for everyone in my family, except the See's chocolates for my grandfather. See's was closed, and I went by Gerrard's as a last ditch effort, but assumed they did not sell See's. Tom was there when I walked in, so I asked him if they sell See's, and he confirmed they didn't. However, after showing me the different chocolate options they had, he left and then came back a few minutes later with his own PERSONAL box of See's candy, and offered it to me to give to my grandpa for Christmas. I accepted, and Tom basically saved Christmas. Go Gerrard's!! Thank you so much Tom.</Review>

I first started shopping here for hard to find beers in their locally famous "Beer Cave" but now I stop by for lunch too. The deli is excellent and it has a wide range of options besides sandwiches. < review>
Great neighborhood market. Lots of specialty products as well as everyday items. Prices are usually the highest in town for most items, but the convenience and products no one else have keep me coming back. They do have good sales and special buys each week. But be ready to use these items right away or freeze as the best sales are usually close to the Sell By date.< /review>

< Time>
1602005848789<//Time>
<rating>4</rating>< text>
I love the Redlands T shirts and caps it offers. Unfortunately there seems to be a price hike  on most items.   Buy 1 get 1 free on uncooked pre packaged meat  uncooked sea food is a good but.. Just be more particular with the  prepackaged buy one get one free already cooked deals. (rice with orange chicken is a  thumbs down) Besides that everything else is good. Gerrard's offer a one of a kind insanely huge international variety of beers. Also you may find many hard to find specialty sodas. They also offer award winning Boar's head soups which includes the ever so scrumptious ,can't get enough of New England Clam chowder. Which by the way is the best clam chowder one can find in the world! (My opinion) Nevertheless Gerrard's is a local town store. They sell local farmers fruits and vegetables. The bakery offers delicious rich danishes muffins, brownies  cookies, cakes to order.  I want to recommend the pineapple upside down danish which is the most addicting to me so far. The staff here are friendly and welcoming. I want to give.my thanks to Gerrard's also for staying open to local residents during the covid 19 epidemic lock down. They quickly placed in sanitizing stations out front and every other safety measure to protect customers and staff. I watched them as an unmovable unflinching force providing for the local citizens of Redlands during a time of uncertainty. They have won my vote , my business,my trust. Closing time is 10pm< /text>

< Review>
It is a private neighborhood market, not a chain, and unique to Redlands. If you are shopping for staples for your pantry, go somewhere else because choices are not so great and prices are not competitive. But in the department  of alcoholic beverages,  deserts, and rare food items this store is hard to surpass. It has 2 "caves" for wine and beer, offering beverages for all tastes and wallets. They have extensive cheese isle. They offer good variety of high quality fish and meats. They bake their own deserts and have a big deli section. They even have their own  outdoor grill for smoked and grilled deli foods.< /Review>
